God of War chronicles the adventure of Kratos, former Greek God of War in exile, and his son Atreus as
they journey through the legendary realms of Norse mythology to fulfill the last wish of the boy's
mother, Faye—to scatter her ashes from the highest mountain in the realms.
Before setting out towards the great mountain of Midgard, Kratos tests the boy's readiness with a
hunt—a test he fails when a chance encounter with a Troll sends him into a rage that brings on a latent
childhood sickness. But after a belligerent Stranger with godlike powers arrives at their door and
provokes a fight with Kratos, they set out on the road, ready or not.
They quickly discover that they had been living under a protection stave, and beyond it, the realm of
Midgard has become a dangerous place full of mythic beasts and undead warriors. Trappings remain of
a human civilization that worshipped the Norse gods—offerings to Odin, statues of Thor, and the
Temple of the Norse God of War, Tyr—but the Desolation has left the land almost devoid of people.
They make allies along the way, largely thanks to Atreus' openness and curiosity. They encounter two
Dwarven master blacksmiths, the estranged brothers Brok (foulmouthed, irascible, and blue) and Sindri
(fastidious and germophobic). In their former partnership, they crafted Mjolnir, the Hammer of Thor,
and the Leviathan Axe, the very weapon now wielded by Kratos. They made it for Faye, and in her honor
they each lend support to Kratos and Atreus on their journey.
They also encounter aWitch of the Woods, who teaches them how to use Tcrr's Temple to travel
between the nine realms. When their path to the Mountain is blocked by a magical barrier, the Witch
directs them to the realm of Alfheim. There, after navigating a dangerous path through a warzone of
Light Elves and Dark Elves, they capture the Bifrost Light that can dispel the barrier.
When finally they reach the mountain's summit, they discover a man imprisoned in a tree there, being
interrogated by the very Stranger whose appearance chased them from home. The prisoner is Mimir, a
former advisor to (and now captive of) Odin, and the Stranger is revealed to be Baldur of the Aesir gods.
Once alone, Mimir breaks the news to Kratos and Atreus that the "highest peak" in the realms isn't in
Midgard at all, but in Jotunheim, long-hidden realm of the so-called "Giants" (or Jotnar). Mimir offers
his counsel and service to Kratos as their journey takes on this new destination—on the condition that
Kratos "frees" Mimir by chopping off his head and finding a way to resurrect it.
The Witch of the Woods is able to bring back Mimir, and it turns out the two are no strangers... for the
Witch is actually the goddess Freya, former leader of the Vanir gods, and Mimir is responsible for
brokering her ill-fated marriage to Odin. Now, confined to Midgard and prevented from fighting by
Odin's curse, she lives in exile as a mortal. Learning this strikes a nerve in Kratos, himself a god in exile,
but one who has refused to tell his son about his true nature (or the shameful, bloody deeds of his past).
Kratos, incensed that Freya did not divulge her godhood, angrily withdraws with Atreus and Mimir's
Head to seek a way to reach Jotunheim and fulfill Faye's wish.
To discover a path to the lost realm of the Giants, Mimir first leads them to talk to Jormungandr, the
World Serpent, the last known Giant left in Midgard. Kratos and Atreus first encountered the serpent
Santa
Monica
Studid
God of War — For WGA Award Consideration only 1
when they arrived in the lake surrounding TNir's Temple, but they could not speak his language. In fact,
none can except for Mimir. Jormungandr tells them where to find the secret travel rune for Jotunheim
and the magical chisel they need to carve it, and they embark on a quest to obtain them.
Along the way, they are attacked by Magni and Modi, sons of Thor and henchmen to their uncle Baldur.
Modi taunts the boy to the point of rage (landing a bit close to home with repeated insults about his
mother). Kratos kills Magni, but Modi survives long enough to ambush them later, provoking Atreus into
a rage that triggers his sickness and leaves him at death's door.
Kratos swallows his pride and takes the boy to Freya to plead for help. Freya forgives him his distrust of
gods, and tells Kratos the ingredient she needs to save the boy can be found only in Helheim, the frozen
realm of the dead where the ice-powers of the Leviathan Axe will be useless. Resigned to digging up his
past, Kratos returns home to retrieve his old weapons stashed there, the fiery Blades of Chaos.
Once Atreus is healed, Kratos heeds the advice of Freya and Mimir, and reveals his true nature to his
son. However, he stops well short of coming clean about his past and the terrible mistakes that the boy
could learn from. As a result of the half-truth, Atreus becomes arrogant in his godhood, disrespecting
their allies, and finally defying his own father by executing a beaten and helpless Modi. They return to
the Mountain summit with the needed elements, but they are in personal discord when Baldur again
attacks. Baldur tries to kidnap Atreus on his dragon, but Kratos jumps on and a chaotic chase ensues.
Ultimately, they wind up back in Helheim, where ghostly visions of their misdeeds help Atreus regain
perspective, and compassion for his father's burdens. They also learn of a connection that Mimir was
bewitched not to reveal—that Freya is Baldur's mother, and that she is the creator of the spell that
renders him indestructible but unable to feel anything.
Working once again as a team, Kratos and Atreus escape Hel, discover an even more secret path to
Jotunheim, and stumble onto the weakness in Baldur's invulnerability. Even "cured" Baldur cannot
forgive Freya and tries to kill her, but Kratos intervenes and kills Baldur, an act for which Freya swears
terrible vengeance. Kratos explains to Atreus that they must break the cycle of godly children killing
their parents and reveals the true extent of his atrocities in Greece, including killing his own father.
At last they open a gate to Jotunheim, leaving Mimir behind with a reunited Brok & Sindri, and they
encounter a shrine for the Giants who fled Midgard. Atreus' touch reveals a hidden carving that
predicted their entire journey. They learn that Faye herself was a Giant, and that she foresaw every step
of the journey that would bring them here, even helping to set it in motion. At the peak, Kratos and
Atreus spread Faye's ashes together, and puzzle over her intent, as well as the reason the Giants'
prophecy refers to Atreus by another name—"Loki."
Upon returning to Midgard, they learn that Baldur's death has prematurely triggered Fimbulwinter, the
beginning of a prophesied cycle leading to Ragnarok. Kratos and Atreus return home to rest, and Atreus
has a vivid vision of a stormy night some years in the future, when Thor appears at their house.

1. THE MARKED TREES
EXT. FOREST IDUNN/NEAR RIVER BANK (MIDGARD) — DAWN
MAIN MENU SCREEN:
KRATOS stands solemnly amidst a Scandinavian forest. His eyes are fixed on a NORTHERN PINE,
specifically on a GOLDEN HANDPRINT adorning the pale bark of the trunk.
The former God of War looks older. Tired. The storm of years has chipped away at his features: Wrinkles
spiderweb out from his eyes, and his beard is brushed with grey. His skin remains ashen, save for the
familiar RED TATTOO that begins below his left eye, winds over his hairless pate and around his arm and
chest. Both of his arms are wrapped in BLOODSTAINED LINEN STRIPS. No other vestige remains of the
Kratos we've known.
In one hand hangs an AXE.
The player selects New Game from the menu, and our story begins...
Kratos KNEELS next to the tree, and puts his fingers tenderly on the shining handprint, the size of a
woman's hand. He leans his head against the trunk, and closes his eyes. He takes a DEEP BREATH before
opening them again.
Kratos stands, takes a step back, and lifts the axe in his hands: THE LEVIATHAN. The blade is etched with
an intricate network of grooves along the metal. This is no ordinary axe; it HUMS, coursing with
mysterious power.
As Kratos chops away at the tree, he seems distracted, lost in thought. Each successive swing is more
powerful, more intense, more angry, than the last... until he's swinging away with an emotional frenzy
that goes well beyond the act of felling a tree. With one last mighty chop, his grunts of effort give way to
a FRIGHTENING ROAR that echoes between the trees for a mile.
KRATOS
RAAAAAAAAAAAAAAA!!
The tree CREAKS and falls, shaking the earth. Kratos stands looking at his handiwork: The trunk is
fractured, but the largest intact piece is suitable for his purposes. He lets the rage pass through him and
dissipate. He holsters the axe on his back, and steps forward to reach for the log.
Kratos stops, noticing a BLOODSTAINED LINEN STRIP hanging from his forearm, shaken loose during his
loss of control, like a piece of him unraveling. He reaches for it... but then he pauses, closing his eyes, as
if at risk of being overwhelmed. Anger he has learned to manage, however imperfectly... but grief and
shame are another matter.

He opens his eyes again, and shakes his head as if embarrassed by his emotions, even when alone. He
begins to tightly rewrap the bloody bandages around the wound that never heals.
ATREUS (0.S.)
I found some.
ATREUS, a PRE-ADOLESCENT BOY—pale, and slight for his age—EMERGES from between the trees,
holding up a MISTLETOE SPRIG. Kratos turns away from him, as if he doesn't want the boy to see his
wounds, and quickly finishes wrapping the bandages.
KRATOS
Get in the boat, boy.
His father's muted response dampens the boy's enthusiasm. He nods and runs down a path toward a
nearby BOAT docked along a RIVER BANK.
Kratos turns back to the felled tree. He picks up the enormous WHITE LOG and lifts it over his shoulder
with relative ease, a reminder of his unnatural strength. He quietly carries the log down the path to the
river, where the two of them LASH the log to the waiting boat and begin to PADDLE downstream.
Dawn is coming. It's too early for songbirds and the only noise is that of small branches giving way, the
crackling of ice, and the river. After a little while, the boy breaks the silence—

body is wrapped in rustic CLOTH, the color of Tiger's Eye, arms crossed over chest. Nestled around the
head is a WREATH of purple flowers. Tucked in the wrappings is a small HUNTING KNIFE.

2. NOT READY
EXT. FOREST IDUNN/RUINED GARDEN (MIDGARD) — DAY (CONTINUOUS)
Working their way home in sullen silence, Kratos and Atreus discover the troll had set fire to the garden
kept by the boy's mother. There they encounter an UNDEAD SOLDIER very unlike the Draugr, armed and
armored, closer in appearance to a living man, but with ICY BLUE TRANSLUCENT SKIN. Frost fills the air
as it lunges for Kratos with its sword.
ATREUS
What IS that thing!?
Kratos deals with the strange attacker, but it's not the last unusual sight on their road home. Finally
Atreus can't help pointing out the troubling signs—
ATREUS
I told you something was different about the forest.
KRATOS
And I told you not to speak.
ATREUS
But why would a Fire Troll burn mother's garden? And
since when are Draugr so close to the house? And what
was that frozen thing that attacked us?
KRATOS
I do not know. Now be silent—we are almost home.

31. EPILOGUE
EXT/INT. GIANT'S FINGERS/SHRINE (JOTUNHEIM) — DAY (CONTINUOUS)

All Spartans are great warriors. We train from birth. Our

Santa
Monica

God of War ©2018 — For WGA Award Consideration only 324
ATREUS

KRATOS

inspired us to hope... that though we were machines of
war, yet there was humanity in us. Goodness. When the
day came for him to lay down his life in battle, his
sacrifice saved countless others, and turned the tide in
our favor. I carried him home on his shield, and buried
him with all the honors of Spartan custom. His memory
was a comfort in dark times.

God of War ©2018 — For WGA Award Consideration only 327
MIMIR'S HEAD
I never had the pleasure. Laufey was a rumor in the
halls of Asgard—a Giantess warrior who thwarted many
an Aesir god's plans. Freeing those who they would
enslave, feeding those who they would starve, generally
making a nuisance of herself in the most noble of ways.
Thor was terribly frustrated he could never find her to
fight. Once my imprisonment began, I could only
wonder what became of her, and who she would turn
out to be. Yours is quite a singular lineage, lad.

FADE TO BLACK
TITLE CARD: "Years Later..."
EXT/INT. FOREST IDUNN/KRATOSI HOUSE (MIDGARD) — NIGHT
A night of sleep is suddenly and violently interrupted by roaring THUNDER and flashing LIGHTNING.
Kratos scrambles to his feet, every muscle on alert. This is no storm.
What was that—?
Your bow..!
ATREUS
KRATOS
He looks to Kratos and they exchange a knowing glance. There will be no hiding in the cellar this time.
Atreus picks up his BOW and QUIVER, silently notching an ARROW. Kratos grabs his AXE from a peg on
the wall, and throws open the front door.
A HOODED FIGURE stands alone in the backyard, unfazed by the crashes of lightning around him.
The camera swings around behind the mysterious figure, settling into a "gunslinger duel" shot, with the
figure's HEAVY CLOAK obscuring the right half of the frame, and Kratos and Atreus facing us on the left.
KRATOS
Who are you?!
He flips the cloak back to reveal the weapon hanging at his side—a HAMMER, furiously rippling with
electric energy. There is no mistaking it—the hammer is MALNIR, and the man bearing it is THOR.
